  380. I received my Spinbrush as part of a product testing panel with Smiley360. Included in the test was also a tube of Arm and Hammer Truly Radiant toothpaste. Having a significant amount of experience with product testing I have spent the last month trying each product with my regular product, i.e. regular toothbrush with the toothpaste, and regular tooth paste with the toothbrush to come up with the best possible determination possible with a single subject.<br /><br />I found the Truly Radiant Toothpaste to be better than the Colgate Whitening I have been using. The plastic used in the construction is very slippery when wet. Brushing teeth is ALWAY going to result in a wet toothbrush handle as the hand is wet to begin with or when the moistened brush is tipped up to put in the mouth moisture immediately makes its way down the handle. This combination of an already slippery handle and water is not a good thing.<br /><br />The slippery issue is compounded with this product as the slide switch to turn the brush on and off is made of the same slippery especially when wet plastic as the handle itself. There is no significant raised area on the switch to give a thumb or finger something substantial to push against to compensate for this. Since the switch triggers motion both spinning and bi-directional of surfaces with toothpaste applied it is definitely ill-advised to turn this device on before it is fully in the mouth.<br /><br />The only remedy I found with the test product was to wrap it in a washcloth to keep the surface dry and provide a better grip and reduce switch slip. I found this completely unsatisfactory as it generated a lot more laundry and mess.<br /><br />I would suggest the manufacturer redesign the handle to use a slip resistant material and the switch for better grip as well. Such a redesign would also make it possible for individuals with arthritis and other impairments of the hand to use the product which the current design would prohibit.

  411. I’ve been using this Spinbrush twice a day for almost three months now. The batteries (Duracell) that came with it just died, so in that regard, this toothbrush gives good bang for its buck. It also deep cleans extremely well. I’ve had some stains on the back of my bottom teeth that I’d been trying to scrub away with a regular toothbrush to no avail. This Spinbrush, however, has lightened them significantly, and without any extra pressure applied than normal brushing.<br /><br />Now for the reason why this brush gets four stars instead of five. The replacement heads are extremely pricey. At about $4.50 apiece, you can get two for the price of a brand new toothbrush *with* batteries. So, in fact, by buying replacement heads, you’re actually losing money. And because it is recommended that heads be replaced every three months, that’s a LOT of money down the drain over time. I can see how this product is a huge moneymaker for Arm & Hammer. Unfortunately, the cost of long-term loyalty has alienated me a bit.<br /><br />Not sure if I’ll fall for the consumer gouging. I really like this brush, but I’ll probably just wait for a sale and buy a brand new product. And that mindset also disturbs me because if everyone takes the same approach, how many of these Spinbrushes are going to end up rotting in landfills? Please consider the environmental effects of your profit model, Arm & Hammer.
